\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wmBox\_sound}, kernel-checked]
If $\mathtt{langBox}\;\mathtt{wmCoreLanguageDef}\;\varphi\;(\mathtt{encodeWM}\;t)$,
then $\varphi(\mathtt{encodeWM}\;t')$ for every
$t' : \mathsf{WMTerm}\;s$ with $\mathsf{WMStep}\;t'\;t$.
\end{theorem}

\noindent
However, the converse---\emph{backward completeness}---is \textbf{false}
for intrinsically sorted terms.
The obstacle is that the Pattern-level reduction system admits
predecessors \emph{outside the image} of $\mathtt{encodeWM}$.
For example, $\mathtt{ruleCombineZero}$ (whose right-hand side is
$\mathtt{.fvar}\;\texttt{"e"}$) produces the Pattern-level predecessor
$\mathtt{pCombine}\;(\mathtt{.fvar}\;\texttt{"x"})\;\mathtt{pEvidenceZero}$
at $\mathtt{.fvar}\;\texttt{"x"}$---but $\mathtt{.fvar}\;\texttt{"x"}$
is the encoding of a \emph{leaf} term ($\mathsf{state}$ or
$\mathsf{query}$), which has no $\mathsf{WMStep}$ predecessor with a
$\mathsf{combine}$ head.

\emph{Restricted to the image} of $\mathsf{encodeWM}$, backward
completeness holds:

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wmBoxOnImage\_iff}, kernel-checked]
\label{thm:box-image}
For $t : \mathsf{WMTerm}\;s$ and any predicate~$\varphi$:
\[
(\forall t'.\; \mathsf{WMStep}\;t'\;t \Rightarrow \varphi(\mathsf{encodeWM}\;t'))
\;\Leftrightarrow\;
\mathsf{langBoxOnImageAt}\;s\;\mathsf{wmCoreLanguageDef}\;\varphi\;
(\mathsf{encodeWM}\;t)
\]
\end{theorem}

\noindent
Here $\mathsf{langBoxOnImageAt}\;s$ quantifies only over Pattern-level
predecessors that are themselves in the sort-$s$ WMTerm image.  This gives
the complete adequacy picture:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lcc}
\toprule
& Forward ($\Diamond$) & Backward ($\Box$) \\
\midrule
Unrestricted & biconditional & sound only \\
Image-restricted & biconditional & \textbf{biconditional} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
See \codepath{Mettapedia/OSLF/Framework/WMCalculusEncoding.lean}
(497~lines, 0~sorry).

%% ---------------------------------------------------------------
\section{The 13-Axis Vertex Family}
\label{sec:wm-vertex-family}
\label{sec:wm-13axis}

The WM calculus variants are indexed by a 13-axis \texttt{WMFullVertex}:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{rlll}
\toprule
\textbf{\#} & \textbf{Axis} & \textbf{Values} & \textbf{Effect} \\
\midrule
1--4 & Base (logic, tv, interval, typing)
     & $2 \times 2 \times 3 \times 2 = 24$
     & model-level (same rules) \\
5 & Overlap & additive $|$ overlapAware & +1 rule \\
6 & Forgetting & none $|$ scopeBased $|$ supportTracked & +2--3 rules \\
7 & Provenance & none $|$ sourceLabeled & +6 rules \\
8 & Fixpoint & none $|$ closure $|$ policy $|$ cascade & +2--4 rules \\
9 & Cost & none $|$ costTracked & +3 rules \\
10 & Conservation & none $|$ conserving & +2 rules \\
11 & Experiment & none $|$ deterministic $|$ stochastic & +3--7 rules \\
12 & Kripke & none $|$ pointedKripke & +3 rules \\
13 & Carrier & concrete $|$ generic & +2 rules \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The first four axes are \emph{model-level}: all 24 combinations produce the
same \texttt{LanguageDef} (the same rewrite rules), differing only in
semantic interpretation.  This is proved by \texttt{wmVertexLanguageDef\_eq}
(exhaustive case analysis, kernel-checked).  The remaining nine axes are
\emph{syntactic}: each adds genuinely new rewrite rules.

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wmFullVertexMinimal\_ruleCount}, kernel-checked]
The minimal vertex (all extensions disabled) has exactly~5 rewrite rules
(the core rules).
\end{theorem}

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wmFullVertexMaximal\_ruleCount}, kernel-checked]
The maximal vertex (all extensions enabled at strongest level) has exactly~36
rewrite rules.
\end{theorem}

\subsection{Extension Families}
\label{sec:wm-extensions}

Each extension family contributes its own rewrite rules:

\paragraph{Overlap (1 rule).}
$\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{OverlapMerge}(W_1, W_2), q)
\;\leadsto\; \mathsf{OverlapCorrect}(\mathsf{Extract}(W_1,q),\;
\mathsf{Extract}(W_2,q),\; \mathsf{OverlapFactor}(W_1,W_2,q))$.

\paragraph{Forgetting (2--3 rules).}
Outside-scope invariance:
$\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{Forget}(S, W), q)
\;\leadsto\; \mathsf{Extract}(W, q)$ (when $q \notin \mathrm{scope}(S)$).
Idempotence:
$\mathsf{Forget}(S, \mathsf{Forget}(S, W)) \;\leadsto\; \mathsf{Forget}(S, W)$.
Support-tracked mode adds the exact-inverse rule.

\paragraph{Provenance (6 rules).}
Source-compatibility symmetry, fallback decomposition (compatible/incompatible
cases), partial revision, trusted-gate identity, and evidence
additivity under compatible fallback revision.

\paragraph{Fixpoint (2--4 rules).}
Closure fixpoint, iteration unfolding, trusted-all simplification (policy mode),
and cardinality-bounded stabilization (cascade mode).

\paragraph{Cost (3 rules).}
Swap anomaly symmetry, swap anomaly zero, and schedule error symmetry.

\paragraph{Conservation (2 rules).}
Anti-hallucination and Noether conservation.

\paragraph{Experiment channels (3--7 rules).}
Experiment evidence additivity, Blackwell factorization pullback, channel
composition identity.  Stochastic mode adds four more rules.

\paragraph{Kripke (3 rules).}
Kripke evidence additivity, singleton satisfaction, and singleton refutation.

\paragraph{Generic carriers (2 rules).}
Generic evidence additivity and query-equivalence transport.

\subsection{Vertex Preorder and Forward Fiber}
\label{sec:wm-vertex-preorder}

The 9~syntactic extension axes each define a total preorder on modes
(more expressive mode $\le$ less expressive mode, following the convention
that $\bot$~=~most rules).  The product of these 9~per-axis preorders
gives a preorder on \texttt{WMFullVertex}:

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wmFullVertexMaximal\_le}, kernel-checked]
For every $w : \mathsf{WMFullVertex}$, the maximal vertex (36~rules)
satisfies $\mathsf{wmFullVertexMaximal} \le w$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wmFullVertex\_le\_minimal}, kernel-checked]
For every $v : \mathsf{WMFullVertex}$, $v \le \mathsf{wmFullVertexMinimal}$
(5~rules).
\end{theorem}

\noindent
Rule-set monotonicity gives \emph{forward transport}: if $v \le w$
(more rules), then every reduction at~$w$ is also a reduction at~$v$.
This is packaged as a \texttt{ForwardFiber} (from
\texttt{HypercubeGSLTFunctor.lean}): a functor from the vertex preorder
category to \texttt{LanguageDef}s with identity forward morphisms.

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wmFullForwardFiber}, kernel-checked]
The function $v \mapsto \mathsf{wmFullVertexLanguageDef}(v)$ is a
\texttt{ForwardFiber} over the \texttt{WMFullVertex} preorder:
every weakness edge $v \le w$ induces a forward morphism with
$\mathsf{mapTerm} = \mathrm{id}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wmFullVertexLanguageDef\_base\_eq}, kernel-checked]
For any two full vertices $v, w$ with identical extension axes (axes~5--13),
$\mathsf{wmFullVertexLanguageDef}(v) = \mathsf{wmFullVertexLanguageDef}(w)$.
The base~4 axes do not affect the rewrite rules.
\end{theorem}

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wmCalc\_transport}, kernel-checked]
For any $v, w : \mathsf{WMVertex}$ and any reduction chain
$p \to^* q$ at vertex~$v$, the same chain is a valid reduction at
vertex~$w$.
\end{theorem}

\noindent
See \codepath{Mettapedia/OSLF/Framework/WMCalculusVertexOrder.lean}
(228~lines, 0~sorry) and
\codepath{Mettapedia/OSLF/Framework/WMCalculusGSLTVertex.lean}.

%% ---------------------------------------------------------------
\section{OSLF Layer: Modal Operators and Semantic Bridge}
\label{sec:wm-oslf-layer}
\label{sec:wm-oslf}
\label{sec:wm-gslt-bridge}

Passing any vertex's \texttt{LanguageDef} through the OSLF pipeline
(\texttt{langOSLF}) automatically derives:

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Diamond ($\Diamond\varphi$)}: holds at pattern~$p$ iff
  $\exists q.\; p \leadsto q \wedge \varphi(q)$.
  ``This WM expression can be rewritten to one satisfying~$\varphi$.''

\item \textbf{Box ($\Box\varphi$)}: holds at pattern~$p$ iff
  $\forall q.\; q \leadsto p \to \varphi(q)$.
  ``All expressions that reduce \emph{to}~$p$ satisfy~$\varphi$.''

\item \textbf{Galois connection} $\Diamond \dashv \Box$
  (\texttt{langGalois}, automatic):
  $(\forall p.\; p \in \Diamond\varphi \Rightarrow p \in \psi)
  \;\Leftrightarrow\;
  (\forall p.\; p \in \varphi \Rightarrow p \in \Box\psi)$.
\end{itemize}

These operators have concrete evidence-theoretic meaning:

\begin{description}
\item[Evidence reachability ($\Diamond$).]
  $\Diamond(\mathsf{isCombined})$ holds at any
  $\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{Revise}(W_1, W_2), q)$ because the
  evidence-add rule rewrites it to a $\mathsf{Combine}$ term.

\item[Evidence safety ($\Box$).]
  $\Box(\mathsf{isPositive})$ at pattern~$p$ means every expression that
  reduces to~$p$ was already positive---a backward safety guarantee.

\item[Vertex dependence.]
  At the minimal vertex (5~rules), $\Diamond$ is small (few rewrites
  reachable).  At the maximal vertex (36~rules), $\Diamond$ is much
  larger.  The Galois connection tightens:
  more $\Diamond$ means weaker~$\Box$.

\item[Conservation as $\Box$-safety.]
  With conservation rules enabled, $\Box(\text{outsideScope} \Rightarrow
  \text{preserved})$ holds at any $\mathsf{Revise}(W, \Delta)$: backward
  safety captures the Noether-style conservation guarantee.
\end{description}

\subsection{Diamond Theorems and Galois Corollaries}

Pattern predicates ($\mathsf{isCombined}$, $\mathsf{isDecomposable}$,
$\mathsf{isFixpoint}$, $\mathsf{isOverlapCorrected}$,
$\mathsf{isZeroEvidence}$, etc.) capture evidence-theoretic properties
syntactically.  Each $\Diamond$~theorem composes a step lemma with a
predicate:

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{diamond\_isCombined\_at\_decomposable}, kernel-checked]
For any WM vertex~$v$ and patterns $W_1, W_2, q$:
$\Diamond(\mathsf{isCombined})$ holds at
$\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{Revise}(W_1, W_2),\; q)$.
\end{theorem}

\noindent
Similar $\Diamond$~theorems hold for all 9~extension axes
(\texttt{full\_diamond\_overlapCorrected},
\texttt{full\_diamond\_closureFixpoint},
\texttt{full\_diamond\_antiHallucination},
\texttt{full\_diamond\_experimentDecomposable},
\texttt{full\_diamond\_kripkeDecomposable},
\texttt{full\_diamond\_genericDecomposable}).

The Galois connection $\Diamond \dashv \Box$ instantiates to concrete
evidence-theoretic dualities:

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wmCalc\_decomposability\_safety}, kernel-checked]
$(\forall p.\; \Diamond(\mathsf{isCombined})(p) \Rightarrow \psi(p))
\;\Leftrightarrow\;
(\forall p.\; \mathsf{isCombined}(p) \Rightarrow \Box(\psi)(p))$.
\end{theorem}

\noindent
Similar corollaries hold for overlap, fixpoint, and conservation predicates.

\subsection{Relational Encoding and Diamond Chaining}

A relational encoding $\mathsf{WMTermEncodes}$ connects abstract
WorldModel terms to OSLF patterns:

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wm\_evidence\_add\_sound}, kernel-checked]
If patterns encode WM terms, then the OSLF evidence-add reduction preserves
encoding: the reduced pattern encodes
$\mathsf{combine}(\mathsf{extract}(t_{W_1}, t_q),\;
\mathsf{extract}(t_{W_2}, t_q))$.
\end{theorem}

Multi-step rewrite chains compose via $\mathsf{LangReducesStar}$:

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{chain\_evidence\_add\_nested}, kernel-checked]
$\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{Revise}(\mathsf{Revise}(W_1, W_2), W_3),\; q)$
reduces in one step to
$\mathsf{Combine}(\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{Revise}(W_1,W_2),\,q),\;
\mathsf{Extract}(W_3,q))$.
Full decomposition via \texttt{chain\_evidence\_add\_fully\_nested}
(\S\ref{sec:wm-algebraic-core}) achieves the two-step result using
congruence closure.
\end{theorem}

\subsection{Evidence Barbs (Process-Algebraic Observables)}

Following Milner's barbed bisimulation, a WM-specific observable:

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wmRevisedState\_evidenceBarb}, kernel-checked]
$\mathsf{Revise}(W_1, W_2)$ exhibits an evidence barb for~$q$ whenever
$\mathsf{Combine}(\mathsf{Extract}(W_1,q), \mathsf{Extract}(W_2,q))$ is
non-zero---the evidence-add rule provides the witness.
\end{theorem}

\subsection{Neighborhood Semantics Fiber}

The abstract LanguageDef reductions correspond exactly to concrete
model-theoretic facts when instantiated at the neighborhood WorldModel
instance (\texttt{PLNWorldModelNeighborhood.lean}):

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{neighborhood\_evidence\_add\_correspondence}, kernel-checked]
The LanguageDef reduction and the mathematical identity
$\mathsf{neighborhoodEvidence}(W_1 + W_2, \varphi) =
\mathsf{neighborhoodEvidence}(W_1, \varphi) +
\mathsf{neighborhoodEvidence}(W_2, \varphi)$
are corresponding facts (both hold simultaneously).
\end{theorem}

\noindent
Further theorems: $\Diamond$~decomposition,
singleton adequacy, evidence barbs, and the Galois corollary
$\Diamond \dashv \Box$ with neighborhood-semantic reading.%
\footnote{Formalized in \codepath{Mettapedia/OSLF/Framework/WMCalculusNeighborhoodBridge.lean}
  (230~lines, 0~sorry).}

\subsection{First-Order Logic Fiber}

The parallel FOL fiber connects the LanguageDef to the Tarskian
WorldModel instance (\texttt{PLNWorldModelFOL.lean}):

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{fol\_evidence\_add\_correspondence}, kernel-checked]
The same evidence-add correspondence holds for Tarskian satisfaction
counting.
\end{theorem}

\noindent
The FOL fiber additionally proves:
\textbf{validity as maximal strength} (query strength equals~1 when all
structures satisfy the query) and a fully faithful
\textbf{model-theoretic consequence bridge} ($\forall S.\; S \models \varphi
\Rightarrow S \models \psi$ iff
$\mathsf{queryStrength}(W, \varphi) \le \mathsf{queryStrength}(W, \psi)$,
with the converse holding at singletons).%
\footnote{Formalized in \codepath{Mettapedia/OSLF/Framework/WMCalculusFOLBridge.lean}
  (295~lines, 0~sorry).}

%% ---------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Native Type Synthesis: What the Type Pass Sees}
\label{sec:wm-ntt-scope}

The Part title ``Natively Typed World Models'' refers to the following
pipeline: each WM vertex produces a \texttt{LanguageDef}, each
\texttt{LanguageDef} produces an OSLF via \texttt{langOSLF}, and each OSLF
produces a native type system via \texttt{langNativeTypeUsing}.  The native
type system classifies WM terms by their rewrite behavior---specifically, by
which rewrite rules are available at that vertex.

Because all 24 base-axis combinations produce the same
\texttt{LanguageDef} (\texttt{wmVertexLanguageDef\_eq}), the pure
OSLF/NTT extraction is blind to the 4~model-level axes:

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{wmVertexNativeType\_eq}, kernel-checked]
For any \texttt{RelationEnv}~$\rho$ and any two base vertices $v, w$:
$\mathsf{langNativeTypeUsing}\;\rho\;(\mathsf{wmVertexLanguageDef}\;v)
\;=\;
\mathsf{langNativeTypeUsing}\;\rho\;(\mathsf{wmVertexLanguageDef}\;w)$.
\end{theorem}

\noindent
The present WM $\to$ NTT pass is therefore \emph{exact for the
9~syntactic axes} and intentionally insensitive to the
4~model-level axes (logic discipline, truth-value granularity,
interval semantics, typing).

\paragraph{Scope and limitations.}
The native type extracted at a given vertex reflects the
\emph{operational} behavior---which rules fire, which reductions are
available, which terms are well-typed with respect to the rewrite system.
It does \emph{not} distinguish between boolean and Heyting logic, or
between point-valued and interval-valued truth values, because these
distinctions live at the semantic interpretation level, not at the rewrite
level.

Richer semantic-axis sensitivity would require a \emph{semantic bundle}
beyond plain \texttt{LanguageDef}---carrying the interval/view/typing/\allowbreak
interpretation data that the rewrite system does not encode.  Such a bundle
would give each of the 4~base axes its own NTT fiber.  This is a genuine
extension point, not a gap: the current theory cleanly separates what NTT
classifies (rewrite behavior) from what it does not (semantic
interpretation).

%% ---------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Compiled BN Inference Bridge}
\label{sec:wm-bn-bridge}

The guarded forgetting rule
$\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{Forget}(S,W), q) \leadsto \mathsf{Extract}(W, q)$
requires a side-condition oracle answering $\mathsf{outsideScope}(S, q)$.
This oracle encodes d-separation: a BN topology determines which
scope/query pairs are outside scope.

\paragraph{Positive theorem.}
Given \emph{any} \texttt{RelationEnv} that satisfies the
$\mathsf{outsideScope}$ premise, the guarded rule fires:

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{guarded\_forget\_of\_dsep}, kernel-checked]
If $\mathsf{OutsideScope}(\rho, L, S, q)$ holds for a
\texttt{RelationEnv}~$\rho$, then
$\mathsf{langReducesUsing}\;\rho\;L\;
(\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{Forget}(S,W), q))\;
(\mathsf{Extract}(W, q))$
for every world-model~$W$.
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{Negative theorem (collider).}
With the empty oracle, the premise evaluates to~$\varnothing$:

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{collider\_premise\_empty}, kernel-checked]
$\mathsf{applyPremisesWithEnv}\;\varnothing\;L\;
[\mathsf{outsideScope}]\;\mathrm{bs} = [\,]$
for any bindings~$\mathrm{bs}$.
No d-separation certificate is available, so the rule is dead code.
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{Completeness.}
In the guarded calculus, $\mathsf{ruleForgetOutsideGuarded}$ is the
\emph{unique} rule whose left-hand side matches
$\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{Forget}(S,W), q)$:

\begin{theorem}[\texttt{forgettingRulesGuarded\_unique\_match}, kernel-checked]
For every rule~$r$ in the guarded forgetting rules,
$\mathsf{matchPattern}(r.\mathit{left},\;
\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{Forget}(S,W), q)) \ne [\,]$
implies $r = \mathsf{ruleForgetOutsideGuarded}$.
\end{theorem}

\noindent
Combined with the negative theorem: under the empty oracle,
$\mathsf{Extract}(\mathsf{Forget}(S,W), q)$ is \emph{irreducible} in
the guarded calculus.
